---
title: "CPU usage around 80% - Clean install of Xubuntu 12.04 on dell mini 10"
date: 2014-03-13
forum: New to Ubuntu
---

### Post by Jimjums on 2014-03-13
Hello Ubuntu forum people,

I just did a clean install of xubuntu 12.04 on my dell mini 10. Managed to get a work around working for the Poulsbo graphics card. I'm sure a lot of you would have heard of the problem and it was a test for me as a first time linux user.

I did the clean install hoping to get the computer running smooth again, and thought xubuntu was a good option. Anyway, right now CPU usage is at 80-90%, firefox is around 40-50%, and taskmanager around 5-10%. Is this normal?

The computer seems functional, but isn't that really high for CPU usage on a fresh install? What could the problem be? Is the computer just too old, need a clean, something with the OS itself or whatever?

Any advice would be greatly appreciated.
Jimjums

---

### Post by matt_symes on 2014-03-13
Hi

I don't have a dell mini 10 and i have no experience of using one, but those stats do seems rather high.

What hardware do you have in the machine ?

Have you had a look to see what processes are running and using up the CPU ?

Kind regards

---

### Post by sudodus on 2014-03-13
Welcome to the Ubuntu Forums :-)

It depends what you are doing with Firefox. If you are watching video, it is not unusual. If you are watching a static page with no animations, it should settle down to a low value after opening the page and displaying text and pictures.

There are light-weight web browsers, for example

Iceweasel, Midori, Opera, Xombrero

If you need a more responsive computer you can also try Lubuntu 13.10, which is lighter than Xubuntu, but also simpler. Try it live, booted from the install drive 'Try without installing', and select the flavour you like the best.

---

### Post by ajgreeny on 2014-03-13
Tell us what is using all that CPU% by running **top** in terminal and, if needed, hitting upper case P to list processes in cpu order.

### Post by matt_symes on 2014-03-13
HI

That's a low spec machine with only 1G ram you have there.

I would look at a lighter version of Linux on that puppy such as, and i think it's been suggested, Lubuntu.

With only 1G of ram you will soon be swapping out memory all over the place and that will slow your system down no end.

Xubuntu is good (i am currently using it) but i would use something lighter. I would also look at lighter applications.

Kind regards

---

Hi

Make a clone of the hard drive using Clonezilla or other cloning software and then, if you have problems, you can up the clone back on the hard drive.

No risk :)

Kind regards
